Code:

        int main(void) {

        /* With some toolchains (MSYS2/mingw for example) the compiler
         * provides various builtins which are not really implemented and
         * fall back to the stdlib where they aren't provided and fail at
         * build/link time. In case the user provides a header, including
         * the header didn't lead to the function being defined, and the
         * function we are checking isn't a builtin itself we assume the
         * builtin is not functional and we just error out. */
        #if !1 && !defined(bswap32) && !0
            #error "No definition for __builtin_bswap32 found in the prefix"
        #endif

        #ifdef __has_builtin
            #if !__has_builtin(__builtin_bswap32)
                #error "__builtin_bswap32 not found"
            #endif
        #elif ! defined(bswap32)
            __builtin_bswap32;
        #endif
        return 0;
        }
-----------

        int main(void) {

        /* With some toolchains (MSYS2/mingw for example) the compiler
         * provides various builtins which are not really implemented and
         * fall back to the stdlib where they aren't provided and fail at
         * build/link time. In case the user provides a header, including
         * the header didn't lead to the function being defined, and the
         * function we are checking isn't a builtin itself we assume the
         * builtin is not functional and we just error out. */
        #if !1 && !defined(clz) && !0
            #error "No definition for __builtin_clz found in the prefix"
        #endif

        #ifdef __has_builtin
            #if !__has_builtin(__builtin_clz)
                #error "__builtin_clz not found"
            #endif
        #elif ! defined(clz)
            __builtin_clz;
        #endif
        return 0;
        }

        int main(void) {

        /* With some toolchains (MSYS2/mingw for example) the compiler
         * provides various builtins which are not really implemented and
         * fall back to the stdlib where they aren't provided and fail at
         * build/link time. In case the user provides a header, including
         * the header didn't lead to the function being defined, and the
         * function we are checking isn't a builtin itself we assume the
         * builtin is not functional and we just error out. */
        #if !1 && !defined(__builtin_ia32_clflushopt) && !1
            #error "No definition for __builtin_ia32_clflushopt found in the prefix"
        #endif

        #ifdef __has_builtin
            #if !__has_builtin(__builtin_ia32_clflushopt)
                #error "__builtin_ia32_clflushopt not found"
            #endif

        int main(void) {

        /* With some toolchains (MSYS2/mingw for example) the compiler
         * provides various builtins which are not really implemented and
         * fall back to the stdlib where they aren't provided and fail at
         * build/link time. In case the user provides a header, including
         * the header didn't lead to the function being defined, and the
         * function we are checking isn't a builtin itself we assume the
         * builtin is not functional and we just error out. */
        #if !1 && !defined(random_r) && !0
            #error "No definition for __builtin_random_r found in the prefix"
        #endif

        #ifdef __has_builtin
            #if !__has_builtin(__builtin_random_r)
                #error "__builtin_random_r not found"
            #endif
        #elif ! defined(random_r)
            __builtin_random_r;
        #endif
        return 0;
        }
-----------

        int main(void) {

        /* With some toolchains (MSYS2/mingw for example) the compiler
         * provides various builtins which are not really implemented and
         * fall back to the stdlib where they aren't provided and fail at
         * build/link time. In case the user provides a header, including
         * the header didn't lead to the function being defined, and the
         * function we are checking isn't a builtin itself we assume the
         * builtin is not functional and we just error out. */
        #if !0 && !defined(wl_display_dispatch_queue_timeout) && !0
            #error "No definition for __builtin_wl_display_dispatch_queue_timeout found in the prefix"
        #endif

        #ifdef __has_builtin
            #if !__has_builtin(__builtin_wl_display_dispatch_queue_timeout)
                #error "__builtin_wl_display_dispatch_queue_timeout not found"
            #endif
        #elif ! defined(wl_display_dispatch_queue_timeout)
            __builtin_wl_display_dispatch_queue_timeout;
        #endif
        return 0;
        }
